with ConfigDef and ConfigKey classes rather than Java annotations. The core framework is defined in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java, which contains: (1) ConfigDef class - the main configuration specification class with a define() method for building configurations, (2) ConfigKey static inner class - represents a single configuration key with metadata like type, documentation, validators, etc., and (3) toHtmlTable() method - generates HTML documentation from configuration definitions. AbstractConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java) is the base class that all configuration classes extend. Configuration documentation is generated using the toHtmlTable() method embedded in ConfigDef. The pattern is used throughout Kafka via 57+ configuration classes across different modules: Producer/Consumer configs (clients module), Broker configs (server/server-common modules), Connect configs (connect module), Streams configs (streams module), Storage configs (storage module), Coordinator configs (group-coordinator, share-coordinator, transaction-coordinator modules), and Raft configs (raft module). Each config class extends AbstractConfig and defines a static CONFIG field using ConfigDef.define() calls to specify all configuration keys with their types, defaults, documentation, validators, and importance levels. This programmatic approach provides compile-time type safety and runtime validation while supporting dynamic documentation generation via the ConfigDef API.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":23045,"cache_read_input_tokens":20013,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":23045},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"8a01ac0e-d407-44ed-bebe-1d5253ed9771","uuid":"2167e4f1-5744-4e74-b1ad-6d23be32b202"}

with ConfigDef and ConfigKey classes rather than Java annotations. The core framework is defined in clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/ConfigDef.java, which contains: (1) ConfigDef class - the main configuration specification class with a define() method for building configurations, (2) ConfigKey static inner class - represents a single configuration key with metadata like type, documentation, validators, etc., and (3) toHtmlTable() method - generates HTML documentation from configuration definitions. AbstractConfig (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/config/AbstractConfig.java) is the base class that all configuration classes extend. Configuration documentation is generated using the toHtmlTable() method embedded in ConfigDef. The pattern is used throughout Kafka via 57+ configuration classes across different modules: Producer/Consumer configs (clients module), Broker configs (server/server-common modules), Connect configs (connect module), Streams configs (streams module), Storage configs (storage module), Coordinator configs (group-coordinator, share-coordinator, transaction-coordinator modules), and Raft configs (raft module). Each config class extends AbstractConfig and defines a static CONFIG field using ConfigDef.define() calls to specify all configuration keys with their types, defaults, documentation, validators, and importance levels. This programmatic approach provides compile-time type safety and runtime validation while supporting dynamic documentation generation via the ConfigDef API.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
